id="cite_ref-mathgene_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mathgene-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pagephd_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pagephd-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Perry_(physicist)" title="Malcolm Perry (physicist)">Malcolm Perry</a><sup id="cite_ref-mathgene_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mathgene-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-perryphd_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perryphd-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marika_Taylor" title="Marika Taylor">Marika Taylor</a><sup id="cite_ref-mathgene_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mathgene-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-taylorphd_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylorphd-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alan_Yuille" title="Alan Yuille">Alan Yuille</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wu_Zhongchao" title="Wu Zhongchao">Wu Zhongchao</a><sup id="cite_ref-mathgene_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mathgene-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wuphd_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wuphd-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>29 others<sup id="cite_ref-mathgene_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mathgene-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hawking.org.uk">hawking<wbr />.org<wbr />.uk</a></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Signature</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Hawkingsig.svg" class="image"><img alt="Hawkingsig.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Hawkingsig.svg/150px-Hawkingsig.svg.png" width="150" height="95" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Hawkingsig.svg/225px-Hawkingsig.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Hawkingsig.svg/300px-Hawkingsig.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="384" data-file-height="243" /></a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Stephen William Hawking</b> <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:100%;"><a href="/wiki/Companion_of_Honour" class="mw-redirect" title="Companion of Honour">CH</a>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Fellow_of_the_Royal_Society" title="Fellow of the Royal Society">FRS</a>&#32;<a href="/wiki/Fellow_of_the_Royal_Society_of_Arts" title="Fellow of the Royal Society of Arts">FRSA</a></span> (8 January 1942 \xe2\x80\x93 14 March 2018) was an English <a href="/wiki/Theoretical_physics" title="Theoretical physics">theoretical physicist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cosmology" title="Cosmology">cosmologist</a>, and author, who was director of research at the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Theoretical_Cosmology" title="Centre for Theoretical Cosmology">Centre for Theoretical Cosmology</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> at the time of his death.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-2_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-3_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-3-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He was the <a href="/wiki/Lucasian_Professor_of_Mathematics" title="Lucasian Professor of Mathematics">Lucasian Professor of Mathematics</a> at the University of Cambridge between 1979 and 2009.\n</p><p>His scientific works included a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Roger_Penrose" title="Roger Penrose">Roger Penrose</a> on <a href="/wiki/Penrose%E2%80%93Hawking_singularity_theorems" title="Penrose\xe2\x80\x93Hawking singularity theorems">gravitational singularity theorems</a> in the framework of <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a> and the theoretical prediction that <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">black holes</a> emit radiation, often called <a href="/wiki/Hawking_radiation" title="Hawking radiation">Hawking radiation</a>. Hawking was the first to set out a theory of cosmology explained by a union of the <a href="/wiki/General_theory_of_relativity" class="mw-redirect" title="General theory of relativity">general theory of relativity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a>. He was a vigorous supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Many-worlds_interpretation" title="Many-worlds interpretation">many-worlds interpretation</a> of quantum mechanics.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking achieved commercial success with several works of <a href="/wiki/Popular_science" title="Popular science">popular science</a> in which he discusses his own theories and cosmology in general. His book <i><a href="/wiki/A_Brief_History_of_Time" title="A Brief History of Time">A Brief History of Time</a></i> appeared on the British <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">Sunday Times</a></i> best-seller list for a record-breaking 237 weeks. Hawking was a <a href="/wiki/Fellow_of_the_Royal_Society" title="Fellow of the Royal Society">fellow of the Royal Society</a> (FRS), a lifetime member of the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Pontifical Academy of Sciences">Pontifical Academy of Sciences</a>, and a recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>, the highest civilian award in the United States. In 2002, Hawking was ranked number 25 in the BBC\'s poll of the <a href="/wiki/100_Greatest_Britons" title="100 Greatest Britons">100 Greatest Britons</a>.\nHawking had a rare early-onset slow-progressing form of <a href="/wiki/Motor_neuron_disease" title="Motor neuron disease">motor neurone disease</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Amyotrophic_lateral_sclerosis" title="Amyotrophic lateral sclerosis">amyotrophic lateral sclerosis</a> "ALS" or <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a>\'s disease) that gradually paralysed him over the decades.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Even after the loss of his speech, he was still able to communicate through a <a href="/wiki/Speech-generating_device" title="Speech-generating device">speech-generating device</a>, initially through use of a hand-held switch, and eventually by using a single cheek muscle. He died on 14 March 2018 at the age of 76.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT=20180314_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT=20180314-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IT-20180314_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IT-20180314-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Early_life"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Early life</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Family"><span tocsection-7"><a href="#1966\xe2\x80\x931975"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">1966\xe2\x80\x931975</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">1990\xe2\x80\x932000</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#2000\xe2\x80\x932018"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">2000\xe2\x80\x932018</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Marriages"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Marriages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Future_of_humanity"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Future of humanity</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#Appearances_in_popular_media"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Appearances in popular media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#Awards_and_honours"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and for Science Communication</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Black_Hole_discovery_dedication"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Black Hole discovery dedication</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Publications"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Publications</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Popular_books"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Popular books</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-28"><a href="#Co-authored"><span class="tocnumber">8.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Co-authored</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-29"><a href="#Forewords"><span class="tocnumber">8.1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Forewords</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Children&#39;s_fiction"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Children\'s fiction</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Films_and_series"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Films and works</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span></h3>\n<p>Hawking was born on 8 January 1942<sup id="cite_ref-whoswho_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a> to Frank (1905\xe2\x80\x931986)<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and Isobel Eileen Hawking (n\xc3\xa9e Walker; 1915\xe2\x80\x932013).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiii,_2_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiii,_2-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201121_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201121-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Hawking\'s mother was born into a family of doctors in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SA_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SA-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> His wealthy paternal great-grandfather, from Yorkshire, had over-extended himself buying farm land and then going bankrupt in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_of_British_Agriculture" title="Great Depression of British Agriculture">great agricultural depression</a> during the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-SA_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SA-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> His paternal great-grandmother saved the family from financial ruin by opening a school in their home.<sup id="cite_ref-SA_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SA-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Despite their families\' financial constraints, both parents attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, where Frank read medicine and Isobel read <a href="/wiki/Philosophy,_Politics_and_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Philosophy, Politics and Economics">Philosophy, Politics and Economics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201121_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201121-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Isobel worked as a secretary for a medical research institute, and Frank was a medical researcher.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201121_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201121-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin20026_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin20026-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Hawking had two younger sisters, Philippa and Mary, and an adopted brother, Edward Frank David (1955\xe2\x80\x932003).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen20052,_5_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen20052,_5-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1950, when Hawking\'s father became head of the division of <a href="/wiki/Parasitology" title="Parasitology">parasitology</a> at the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Medical_Research" title="National Institute for Medical Research">National Institute for Medical Research</a>, the family moved to <a href="/wiki/St_Albans" title="St Albans">St Albans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiii_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiii-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In St Albans, the family was considered highly intelligent and somewhat eccentric;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200212_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200212-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> meals were often spent with each person silently reading a book.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> They lived a frugal existence in a large, cluttered, and poorly maintained house and travelled in a converted London taxicab.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122\xe2\x80\x9323_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122\xe2\x80\x9323-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200211\xe2\x80\x9312_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200211\xe2\x80\x9312-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> During one of Hawking\'s father\'s frequent absences working in Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200213_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200213-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> the rest of the family spent four months in <a href="/wiki/Majorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Majorca">Majorca</a> visiting his mother\'s friend Beryl and her husband, the poet <a href="/wiki/Robert_Graves" title="Robert Graves">Robert Graves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen20053_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen20053-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_and_secondary_school_years">Primary and secondary school years</span></h3>\n<p>Hawking began his schooling at the Byron House School in <a href="/wiki/Highgate" title="Highgate">Highgate</a>, London. He later blamed its "<a href="/wiki/Progressive_education" title="Progressive education">progressive methods</a>" for his failure to learn to read while at the school.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In St Albans, the eight-year-old Hawking attended <a href="/wiki/St_Albans_High_School_for_Girls" title="St Albans High School for Girls">St Albans High School for Girls</a> for a few months. At that time, younger boys could attend one of the houses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen20053_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen20053-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201124_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201124-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking attended two <a href="/wiki/Independent_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Independent school (United Kingdom)">independent (i.e. fee-paying) schools</a>, first Radlett School<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201124_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201124-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and from September 1952, <a href="/wiki/St_Albans_School,_Hertfordshire" title="St Albans School, Hertfordshire">St Albans School</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-whoswho_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin20028_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin20028-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> after passing the <a href="/wiki/Eleven-plus" title="Eleven-plus">eleven-plus</a> a year early.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The family placed a high value on education.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201122-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Hawking\'s father wanted his son to attend the well-regarded <a href="/wiki/Westminster_School" title="Westminster School">Westminster School</a>, but the 13-year-old Hawking was ill on the day of the scholarship examination. His family could not afford the school fees without the financial aid of a scholarship, so Hawking remained at St Albans.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin20027\xe2\x80\x938_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin20027\xe2\x80\x938-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen20054_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen20054-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> A positive consequence was that Hawking remained with a close group of friends with whom he enjoyed board games, the manufacture of fireworks, model aeroplanes and boats,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201125\xe2\x80\x9326_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201125\xe2\x80\x9326-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and long discussions about Christianity and <a href="/wiki/Extrasensory_perception" title="Extrasensory perception">extrasensory perception</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200214\xe2\x80\x9316_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200214\xe2\x80\x9316-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> From 1958 on, with the help of the mathematics teacher <a href="/wiki/Dikran_Tahta" title="Dikran Tahta">Dikran Tahta</a>, they built a computer from clock parts, an old telephone switchboard and other recycled components.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201126_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201126-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200219\xe2\x80\x9320_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200219\xe2\x80\x9320-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although known at school as "Einstein", Hawking was not initially successful academically.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201125_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201125-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> With time, he began to show considerable aptitude for scientific subjects and, inspired by Tahta, decided to read mathematics at university.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200217\xe2\x80\x9318_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200217\xe2\x80\x9318-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201127_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201127-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-5_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-5-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Hawking\'s father advised him to study medicine, concerned that there were few jobs for mathematics graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200241_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200241-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> He also wanted his son to attend <a href="/wiki/University_College,_Oxford" title="University College, Oxford">University College, Oxford</a>, his own <i><a href="/wiki/Alma_mater" title="Alma mater">alma mater</a></i>. As it was not possible to read mathematics there at the time, Hawking decided to study physics and chemistry. Despite his headmaster\'s advice to wait until the next year, Hawking was awarded a scholarship after taking the examinations in March 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201127\xe2\x80\x9328_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201127\xe2\x80\x9328-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200242\xe2\x80\x9343_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200242\xe2\x80\x9343-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_years">Undergraduate years</span></h3>\n<p>Hawking began his university education at <a href="/wiki/University_College,_Oxford" title="University College, Oxford">University College, Oxford</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-whoswho_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> in October 1959 at the age of 17.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201128_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201128-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> For the first 18 months, he was bored and lonely&#160;&#8211;&#32;he found the academic work "ridiculously easy".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201128\xe2\x80\x9329_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201128\xe2\x80\x9329-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200246\xe2\x80\x9347,_51_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200246\xe2\x80\x9347,_51-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> His physics tutor, Robert Berman, later said, "It was only necessary for him to know that something could be done, and he could do it without looking to see how other people did it."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201129_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201129-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> A change occurred during his second and third year when, according to Berman, Hawking made more of an effort "to be one of the boys". He developed into a popular, lively and witty college member, interested in classical music and science fiction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201128_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201128-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Part of the transformation resulted from his decision to join the college boat club, the <a href="/wiki/University_College_Boat_Club_(Oxford)" title="University College Boat Club (Oxford)">University College Boat Club</a>, where he <a href="/wiki/Coxswain_(rowing)" title="Coxswain (rowing)">coxed</a> a rowing crew.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201130\xe2\x80\x9331_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201130\xe2\x80\x9331-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHawking1992p._44_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHawking1992p._44-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The rowing coach at the time noted that Hawking cultivated a daredevil image, steering his crew on risky courses that led to damaged boats.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200250_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200250-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201130\xe2\x80\x9331_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201130\xe2\x80\x9331-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking estimated that he studied about 1,000 hours during his three years at Oxford. These unimpressive study habits made sitting his <a href="/wiki/Final_examination" title="Final examination">finals</a> a challenge, and he decided to answer only <a href="/wiki/Theoretical_physics" title="Theoretical physics">theoretical physics</a> questions rather than those requiring factual knowledge. A <a href="/wiki/British_undergraduate_degree_classification" title="British undergraduate degree classification">first-class honours degree</a> was a condition of acceptance for his planned graduate study in <a href="/wiki/Cosmology" title="Cosmology">cosmology</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200253_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200253-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Anxious, he slept poorly the night before the examinations, and the final result was on the borderline between first- and second-class honours, making a <i><a href="/wiki/Oral_exam" title="Oral exam">viva</a></i> (oral examination) necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200254_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200254-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Hawking was concerned that he was viewed as a lazy and difficult student. So, when asked at the oral<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to describe his plans, he said, "If you award me a First, I will go to Cambridge. If I receive a Second, I shall stay in Oxford, so I expect you will give me a First."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200254\xe2\x80\x9355_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200254\xe2\x80\x9355-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> He was held in higher regard than he believed; as Berman commented, the examiners "were intelligent enough to realise they were talking to someone far cleverer than most of themselves".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> After receiving a <a href="/wiki/First_Class_Honours#First-class_honours" class="mw-redirect" title="First Class Honours">first-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Honours_degree" title="Honours degree">BA (Hons.) degree</a> in physics and completing a trip to <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> with a friend, he began his graduate work at <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Hall,_Cambridge" title="Trinity Hall, Cambridge">Trinity Hall, Cambridge</a>, in October 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-whoswho_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whoswho-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200256_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200256-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131\xe2\x80\x9332_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201131\xe2\x80\x9332-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_years">Graduate years</span></h3>\n<p>Hawking\'s first year as a doctoral student was difficult. He was initially disappointed to find that he had been assigned <a href="/wiki/Dennis_William_Sciama" class="mw-redirect" title="Dennis William Sciama">Dennis William Sciama</a>, one of the founders of modern cosmology, as a supervisor rather than noted Yorkshire astronomer <a href="/wiki/Fred_Hoyle" title="Fred Hoyle">Fred Hoyle</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201133_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201133-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200258_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200258-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> and he found his training in mathematics inadequate for work in <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a> and cosmology.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201133\xe2\x80\x9334_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201133\xe2\x80\x9334-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> After being diagnosed with motor neurone disease, Hawking fell into a depression&#160;&#8211;&#32;though his doctors advised that he continue with his studies, he felt there was little point.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200261\xe2\x80\x9363_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200261\xe2\x80\x9363-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> His disease progressed more slowly than doctors had predicted. Although Hawking had difficulty walking unsupported, and his speech was almost unintelligible, an initial diagnosis that he had only two years to live proved unfounded. With Sciama\'s encouragement, he returned to his work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201136_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201136-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200269\xe2\x80\x9370_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200269\xe2\x80\x9370-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Hawking started developing a reputation for brilliance and brashness when he publicly challenged the work of Fred Hoyle and his student <a href="/wiki/Jayant_Narlikar" title="Jayant Narlikar">Jayant Narlikar</a> at a lecture in June 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201142_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201142-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200268\xe2\x80\x9369_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200268\xe2\x80\x9369-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When Hawking began his graduate studies, there was much debate in the physics community about the prevailing theories of the creation of the universe: the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">Big Bang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steady_State_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Steady State theory">Steady State</a> theories.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201134_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201134-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Inspired by <a href="/wiki/Roger_Penrose" title="Roger Penrose">Roger Penrose</a>\'s theorem of a <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">spacetime</a> singularity in the centre of black holes, Hawking applied the same thinking to the entire universe; and, during 1965, he wrote his thesis on this topic.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200271\xe2\x80\x9372_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200271\xe2\x80\x9372-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Hawking\'s thesis<sup id="cite_ref-hawkingphd_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hawkingphd-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> was approved in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-hawkingphd_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hawkingphd-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> There were other positive developments: Hawking received a research fellowship at <a href="/wiki/Gonville_and_Caius_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Gonville and Caius College">Gonville and Caius College</a> at Cambridge;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201143\xe2\x80\x9344_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201143\xe2\x80\x9344-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> he obtained his PhD degree in applied mathematics and theoretical physics, specialising in general relativity and cosmology, in March 1966;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201147_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201147-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> and his essay "Singularities and the Geometry of Space-Time" shared top honours with one by Penrose to win that year\'s prestigious <a href="/wiki/Adams_Prize" title="Adams Prize">Adams Prize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xix_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xix-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201147_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201147-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>\n<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks plainlist" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#ddd8e7;text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Observational_cosmology" title="Observational cosmology">Experiments</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Black_Hole_Initiative" title="Black Hole Initiative">Black Hole Initiative (BHI)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/BOOMERanG_experiment" title="BOOMERanG experiment">BOOMERanG</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cosmic_Background_Explorer" title="Cosmic Background Explorer">Cosmic Background Explorer (COBE)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Illustris_project" title="Illustris project">Illustris project</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Planck_(spacecraft)" title="Planck (spacecraft)">Planck space observatory</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sloan_Digital_Sky_Survey" title="Sloan Digital Sky Survey">Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/2dF_Galaxy_Redshift_Survey" title="2dF Galaxy Redshift Survey">2dF Galaxy Redshift Survey ("2dF")</a></li>\n<li><div style="padding:0.2em 0.4em; line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Wilkinson_Microwave_Anisotropy_Probe" title="Wilkinson Microwave Anisotropy Probe">Wilkinson Microwave Anisotropy<br />Probe (WMAP)</a></div></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#ddd8e7;text-align:center;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_cosmologists" title="List of cosmologists">Scientists</a></li></ul></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center"><div class="hlist" style="padding:0 0.9em;">\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marc_Aaronson" title="Marc Aaronson">Aaronson</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hannes_Alfv%C3%A9n" title="Hannes Alfv\xc3\xa9n">Alfv\xc3\xa9n</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ralph_Asher_Alpher" title="Ralph Asher Alpher">Alpher</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Somnath_Bharadwaj" title="Somnath Bharadwaj">Bharadwaj</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Copernicus</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Willem_de_Sitter" title="Willem de Sitter">de Sitter</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_H._Dicke" title="Robert H. Dicke">Dicke</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Ehlers" title="J\xc3\xbcrgen Ehlers">Ehlers</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Einstein</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_F._R._Ellis" title="George F. R. Ellis">Ellis</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Friedmann" title="Alexander Friedmann">Friedman</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_Gamow" title="George Gamow">Gamow</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alan_Guth" title="Alan Guth">Guth</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Hawking</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edwin_Hubble" title="Edwin Hubble">Hubble</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Georges_Lema%C3%AEtre" title="Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre">Lema\xc3\xaetre</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Andrei_Linde" title="Andrei Linde">Linde</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_C._Mather" title="John C. Mather">Mather</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Newton</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roger_Penrose" title="Roger Penrose">Penrose</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Arno_Allan_Penzias" title="Arno Allan Penzias">Penzias</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vera_Rubin" title="Vera Rubin">Rubin</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brian_Schmidt" title="Brian Schmidt">Schmidt</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_Smoot" title="George Smoot">Smoot</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Alexei_Starobinsky" title="Alexei Starobinsky">Starobinsky</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Steinhardt" title="Paul Steinhardt">Steinhardt</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nicholas_B._Suntzeff" title="Nicholas B. Suntzeff">Suntzeff</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rashid_Sunyaev" title="Rashid Sunyaev">Sunyaev</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_C._Tolman" title="Richard C. Tolman">Tolman</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Woodrow_Wilson" title="Robert Woodrow Wilson">Wilson</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yakov_Borisovich_Zel%27dovich" title="Yakov Borisovich Zel&#39;dovich">Zel\'dovich</a></li>\n</div></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">\n<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:#ddd8e7;text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Physical_cosmology#Subject_history" title="Physical cosmology">Subject history</a></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">\n<ul><li><div style="padding:0.2em 0.4em; line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Discovery_of_cosmic_microwave_background_radiation" title="Discovery of cosmic microwave background radiation">Discovery of cosmic microwave<br />background radiation</a></div></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Big_Bang_theory" title="History of the Big Bang theory">History of the Big Bang theory</a></li>\n<li><div style="padding:0.2em 0.4em; line-height:1.2em;"><a href="/wiki/Religious_interpretations_of_the_Big_Bang_theory" title="Religious interpretations of the Big Bang theory">Religious interpretations of<br />the Big Bang theory</a></div></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_cosmological_theories" title="Timeline of cosmological theories">Timeline of cosmological theories</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; border-bottom: 1px solid #aaa;display:block;margin-top:0.4em; line-height:1.6em;padding-bottom:0.5em;">\n<ul><li><img alt="Category" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/16px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png" title="Category" width="16" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/24px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/48/Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg/32px-Folder_Hexagonal_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="36" data-file-height="31" />&#160;<a href="/wiki/Category:Physical_cosmology" title="Category:Physical cosmology">Category</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/File:Ilc_9yr_moll4096.png" class="image"><img alt="Ilc 9yr moll4096.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ilc_9yr_moll4096.png/16px-Ilc_9yr_moll4096.png" width="16" height="8" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ilc_9yr_moll4096.png/24px-Ilc_9yr_moll4096.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ilc_9yr_moll4096.png/32px-Ilc_9yr_moll4096.png 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2048" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Cosmology" title="Portal:Cosmology">Cosmology&#32;portal</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/File:Crab_Nebula.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Crab Nebula.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Crab_Nebula.jpg/16px-Crab_Nebula.jpg" width="16" height="16" class="noviewer" data-file-width="3864" data-file-height="3864" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Astronomy" title="Portal:Astronomy">Astronomy&#32;portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Physical_cosmology" title="Template:Physical cosmology"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Physical_cosmology" title="Template talk:Physical cosmology"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Physical_cosmology&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span id="1966.E2.80.931975"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1966\xe2\x80\x931975">1966\xe2\x80\x931975</span></h3>\n<p>In his work, and in collaboration with Penrose, Hawking extended the <a href="/wiki/Penrose%E2%80%93Hawking_singularity_theorems" title="Penrose\xe2\x80\x93Hawking singularity theorems">singularity theorem</a> concepts first explored in his doctoral thesis. This included not only the existence of singularities but also the theory that the universe might have started as a singularity. Their joint essay was the runner-up in the 1968 <a href="/wiki/Gravity_Research_Foundation" title="Gravity Research Foundation">Gravity Research Foundation</a> competition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002101_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002101-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201161,_64_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201161,_64-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In 1970 they published a proof that if the universe obeys <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">the general theory of relativity</a> and fits any of the <a href="/wiki/Friedmann_equations" title="Friedmann equations">models</a> of <a href="/wiki/Physical_cosmology" title="Physical cosmology">physical cosmology</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Friedmann" title="Alexander Friedmann">Alexander Friedmann</a>, then it must have begun as a singularity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201164\xe2\x80\x9365_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201164\xe2\x80\x9365-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002115\xe2\x80\x9316_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002115\xe2\x80\x9316-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-7_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-7-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In 1969, Hawking accepted a specially created Fellowship for Distinction in Science to remain at Caius.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201149_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201149-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1970, Hawking postulated what became known as <a href="/wiki/Second_law_of_black_hole_mechanics" class="mw-redirect" title="Second law of black hole mechanics">the second law of black hole dynamics</a>, that the event horizon of a black hole can never get smaller.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201165\xe2\x80\x9367_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201165\xe2\x80\x9367-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> With <a href="/wiki/James_M._Bardeen" title="James M. Bardeen">James M. Bardeen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Carter" title="Brandon Carter">Brandon Carter</a>, he proposed the four <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_black_hole_mechanics" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws of black hole mechanics">laws of black hole mechanics</a>, drawing an analogy with <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamics" title="Thermodynamics">thermodynamics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200538_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200538-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> To Hawking\'s irritation, <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Bekenstein" title="Jacob Bekenstein">Jacob Bekenstein</a>, a graduate student of <a href="/wiki/John_Archibald_Wheeler" title="John Archibald Wheeler">John Wheeler</a>, went further\xe2\x80\x94and ultimately correctly\xe2\x80\x94to apply thermodynamic concepts literally.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201167\xe2\x80\x9368_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201167\xe2\x80\x9368-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002123\xe2\x80\x9324_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002123\xe2\x80\x9324-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In the early 1970s, Hawking\'s work with Carter, Werner Israel and David C. Robinson strongly supported Wheeler\'s <a href="/wiki/No-hair_theorem" title="No-hair theorem">no-hair theorem</a>, one that states that no matter what the original material from which a black hole is created, it can be completely described by the properties of <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">mass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_charge" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical charge">electrical charge</a> and rotation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200533_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200533-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HawkingIsrael1989_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HawkingIsrael1989-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> His essay titled "Black Holes" won the <a href="/wiki/Gravity_Research_Foundation" title="Gravity Research Foundation">Gravity Research Foundation</a> Award in January 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200535_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200535-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Hawking\'s first book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Large_Scale_Structure_of_Space-Time" title="The Large Scale Structure of Space-Time">The Large Scale Structure of Space-Time</a>,</i> written with <a href="/wiki/George_Francis_Rayner_Ellis" class="mw-redirect" title="George Francis Rayner Ellis">George Ellis</a>, was published in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201168_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201168-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Beginning in 1973, Hawking moved into the study of <a href="/wiki/Quantum_gravity" title="Quantum gravity">quantum gravity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200539_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200539-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201168_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201168-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> His work in this area was spurred by a visit to Moscow and discussions with <a href="/wiki/Yakov_Borisovich_Zel%27dovich" title="Yakov Borisovich Zel&#39;dovich">Yakov Borisovich Zel\'dovich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Starobinsky" title="Alexei Starobinsky">Alexei Starobinsky</a>, whose work showed that according to the <a href="/wiki/Uncertainty_principle" title="Uncertainty principle">uncertainty principle</a>, rotating black holes emit particles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002146_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002146-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> To Hawking\'s annoyance, his much-checked calculations produced findings that contradicted his second law, which claimed black holes could never get smaller,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201170_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201170-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> and supported Bekenstein\'s reasoning about their <a href="/wiki/Black_hole_entropy" class="mw-redirect" title="Black hole entropy">entropy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200541_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200541-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002146_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002146-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> His results, which Hawking presented from 1974, showed that black holes emit radiation, known today as <a href="/wiki/Hawking_radiation" title="Hawking radiation">Hawking radiation</a>, which may continue until they exhaust their energy and <a href="/wiki/Black_hole#Evaporation" title="Black hole">evaporate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-9_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-9-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-10_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-10-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201169\xe2\x80\x9373_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201169\xe2\x80\x9373-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Initially, Hawking radiation was controversial. By the late 1970s and following the publication of further research, the discovery was widely accepted as a significant breakthrough in theoretical physics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201170\xe2\x80\x9374_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201170\xe2\x80\x9374-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200542\xe2\x80\x9343_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200542\xe2\x80\x9343-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002150\xe2\x80\x9351_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002150\xe2\x80\x9351-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Hawking was elected a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Fellows_of_the_Royal_Society_elected_in_1974" title="List of Fellows of the Royal Society elected in 1974">Fellow of the Royal Society (FRS) in 1974</a>, a few weeks after the announcement of Hawking radiation. At the time, he was one of the youngest scientists to become a Fellow.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200544_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200544-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002133_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002133-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking was appointed to the Sherman Fairchild Distinguished visiting professorship at the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">California Institute of Technology</a> (Caltech) in 1970. He worked with a friend on the faculty, <a href="/wiki/Kip_Thorne" title="Kip Thorne">Kip Thorne</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201182,_86_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201182,_86-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> and engaged him in a <a href="/wiki/Scientific_wager" title="Scientific wager">scientific wager</a> about whether the <a href="/wiki/Astrophysical_X-ray_source" title="Astrophysical X-ray source">X-ray source</a> <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_X-1" title="Cygnus X-1">Cygnus X-1</a> was a black hole. The wager was an "insurance policy" against the proposition that black holes did not exist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201186\xe2\x80\x9388_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201186\xe2\x80\x9388-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Hawking acknowledged that he had lost the bet in 1990, a bet that was the first of several he was to make with Thorne and others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011150,189,_219_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011150,189,_219-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Hawking had maintained ties to Caltech, spending a month there almost every year since this first visit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201195_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201195-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1975.E2.80.931990"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1975\xe2\x80\x931990">1975\xe2\x80\x931990</span></h3>\n<p>Hawking returned to Cambridge in 1975 to a more academically senior post, as <a href="/wiki/Reader_(academic_rank)" title="Reader (academic rank)">reader</a> in gravitational physics. The mid to late 1970s were a period of growing public interest in black holes and the physicists who were studying them. Hawking was regularly interviewed for print and television.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201190_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201190-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002132\xe2\x80\x9333_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002132\xe2\x80\x9333-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> He also received increasing academic recognition of his work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In 1975, he was awarded both the <a href="/wiki/Eddington_Medal" title="Eddington Medal">Eddington Medal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Pontifical Academy of Sciences">Pius XI Gold Medal</a>, and in 1976 the <a href="/wiki/Dannie_Heineman_Prize_for_Mathematical_Physics" title="Dannie Heineman Prize for Mathematical Physics">Dannie Heineman Prize</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Maxwell Prize">Maxwell Prize</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hughes_Medal" title="Hughes Medal">Hughes Medal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002162_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002162-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xv_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xv-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> He was appointed a professor with a chair in <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_physics" class="mw-redirect" title="Gravitational physics">gravitational physics</a> in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201191_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201191-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The following year he received the <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein_Medal" title="Albert Einstein Medal">Albert Einstein Medal</a> and an honorary doctorate from the University of Oxford.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiv_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiv-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1979, Hawking was elected <a href="/wiki/Lucasian_Professor_of_Mathematics" title="Lucasian Professor of Mathematics">Lucasian Professor of Mathematics</a> at the University of Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lucasian_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lucasian-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> His inaugural lecture in this role was titled: "Is the End in Sight for Theoretical Physics?" and proposed <a href="/wiki/N%3D8_Supergravity" title="N=8 Supergravity">N=8 Supergravity</a> as the leading theory to solve many of the outstanding problems physicists were studying.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201193\xe2\x80\x9394_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201193\xe2\x80\x9394-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> His promotion coincided with a health crisis which led to his accepting, albeit reluctantly, some nursing services at home.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192\xe2\x80\x9393_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192\xe2\x80\x9393-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, he was also making a transition in his approach to physics, becoming more intuitive and speculative rather than insisting on mathematical proofs. "I would rather be right than rigorous", he told Kip Thorne.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201196_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201196-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In 1981, he proposed that information in a black hole is irretrievably lost when a black hole evaporates. This <a href="/wiki/Black_hole_information_paradox" title="Black hole information paradox">information paradox</a> violates the fundamental tenet of quantum mechanics, and led to years of debate, including "<a href="/wiki/The_Black_Hole_War" title="The Black Hole War">the Black Hole War</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Susskind" title="Leonard Susskind">Leonard Susskind</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerard_%27t_Hooft" title="Gerard &#39;t Hooft">Gerard \'t Hooft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201196\xe2\x80\x93101_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201196\xe2\x80\x93101-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Susskind2008_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Susskind2008-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Inflation_(cosmology)" title="Inflation (cosmology)">Cosmological inflation</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;a theory proposing that following the Big Bang, the universe initially expanded incredibly rapidly before settling down to a slower expansion&#160;&#8211;&#32;was proposed by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Guth" title="Alan Guth">Alan Guth</a> and also developed by <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Linde" title="Andrei Linde">Andrei Linde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011108\xe2\x80\x9311_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011108\xe2\x80\x9311-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Following a conference in Moscow in October 1981, Hawking and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Gibbons" title="Gary Gibbons">Gary Gibbons</a> organised a three-week Nuffield Workshop in the summer of 1982 on "The Very Early Universe" at Cambridge University, a workshop that focused mainly on inflation theory.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011111\xe2\x80\x9314_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011111\xe2\x80\x9314-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-12_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-12-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-13_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-13-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Hawking also began a new line of quantum theory research into the origin of the universe. In 1981 at a Vatican conference, he presented work suggesting that there might be no boundary&#160;&#8211;&#32;or beginning or ending&#160;&#8211;&#32;to the universe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011102\xe2\x80\x93103_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011102\xe2\x80\x93103-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002180_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002180-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> He subsequently developed the research in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/James_Hartle" title="James Hartle">Jim Hartle</a>, and in 1983 they published a model, known as the <a href="/wiki/Hartle%E2%80%93Hawking_state" title="Hartle\xe2\x80\x93Hawking state">Hartle\xe2\x80\x93Hawking state</a>. It proposed that prior to the <a href="/wiki/Planck_epoch" class="mw-redirect" title="Planck epoch">Planck epoch</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">universe</a> had no boundary in space-time; before the Big Bang, time did not exist and the concept of the beginning of the universe is meaningless.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-14_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-14-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The initial singularity of the classical Big Bang models was replaced with a region akin to the North Pole. One cannot travel north of the North Pole, but there is no boundary there&#160;&#8211;&#32;it is simply the point where all north-running lines meet and end.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaird2007p._234_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaird2007p._234-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002180\xe2\x80\x9383_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002180\xe2\x80\x9383-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Initially, the no-boundary proposal predicted a <a href="/wiki/Shape_of_the_universe" title="Shape of the universe">closed universe</a>, which had implications about the existence of God. As Hawking explained, "If the universe has no boundaries but is self-contained... then God would not have had any freedom to choose how the universe began."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011129_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011129-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking did not rule out the existence of a Creator, asking in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Brief_History_of_Time" title="A Brief History of Time">A Brief History of Time</a></i> "Is the unified theory so compelling that it brings about its own existence?"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011130_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011130-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In his early work, Hawking spoke of God in a metaphorical sense. In <i>A Brief History of Time</i> he wrote: "If we discover a complete theory, it would be the ultimate triumph of human reason&#160;&#8211;&#32;for then we should know the mind of God."<sup id="cite_ref-sample_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sample-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In the same book he suggested that the existence of God was not necessary to explain the origin of the universe. Later discussions with <a href="/wiki/Neil_Turok" title="Neil Turok">Neil Turok</a> led to the realisation that the existence of God was also compatible with an open universe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYulsman2003pp.&amp;nbsp;174\xe2\x80\x93176_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYulsman2003pp.&amp;nbsp;174\xe2\x80\x93176-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Further work by Hawking in the area of <a href="/wiki/Arrow_of_time" title="Arrow of time">arrows of time</a> led to the 1985 publication of a paper theorising that if the no-boundary proposition were correct, then when the universe stopped expanding and eventually collapsed, time would run backwards.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011180\xe2\x80\x93182_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011180\xe2\x80\x93182-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> A paper by Don Page and independent calculations by <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Laflamme" title="Raymond Laflamme">Raymond Laflamme</a> led Hawking to withdraw this concept.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011182_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011182-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Honours continued to be awarded: in 1981 he was awarded the American <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Medal" title="Franklin Medal">Franklin Medal</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002274_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002274-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> and in the <a href="/wiki/1982_New_Year_Honours" title="1982 New Year Honours">1982 New Year Honours</a> appointed a <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005x\xe2\x80\x93xix_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005x\xe2\x80\x93xix-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011114_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011114-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> These awards did not significantly change Hawking\'s financial status, and motivated by the need to finance his children\'s education and home expenses, he decided in 1982 to write a popular book about the universe that would be accessible to the general public.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011134\xe2\x80\x9335_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011134\xe2\x80\x9335-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002205,_220\xe2\x80\x9321_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002205,_220\xe2\x80\x9321-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Instead of publishing with an academic press, he signed a contract with <a href="/wiki/Bantam_Books" title="Bantam Books">Bantam Books</a>, a mass market publisher, and received a large advance for his book.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011134_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011134-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002220\xe2\x80\x9327_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002220\xe2\x80\x9327-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> A first draft of the book, called <i>A Brief History of Time</i>, was completed in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011135_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011135-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the first messages Hawking produced with his <a href="/wiki/Speech-generating_device" title="Speech-generating device">speech-generating device</a> was a request for his assistant to help him finish writing <i>A Brief History of Time</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011137_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011137-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Peter Guzzardi, his editor at Bantam, pushed him to explain his ideas clearly in non-technical language, a process that required many revisions from an increasingly irritated Hawking.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011140\xe2\x80\x9342_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011140\xe2\x80\x9342-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> The book was published in April 1988 in the US and in June in the UK, and it proved to be an extraordinary success, rising quickly to the top of best-seller lists in both countries and remaining there for months.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011143_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011143-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002243\xe2\x80\x9345_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002243\xe2\x80\x9345-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-g2009_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-g2009-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The book was translated into many languages,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011143\xe2\x80\x9344_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011143\xe2\x80\x9344-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> and ultimately sold an estimated 9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-g2009_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-g2009-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Media attention was intense,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011143\xe2\x80\x9344_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011143\xe2\x80\x9344-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> and a <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> magazine cover and a television special both described him as "Master of the Universe".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011146_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011146-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Success led to significant financial rewards, but also the challenges of celebrity status.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011145\xe2\x80\x9346_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011145\xe2\x80\x9346-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Hawking travelled extensively to promote his work, and enjoyed partying and dancing into the small hours.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011143\xe2\x80\x9344_157-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011143\xe2\x80\x9344-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> A difficulty refusing the invitations and visitors left him limited time for work and his students.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011149_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011149-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Some colleagues were resentful of the attention Hawking received, feeling it was due to his disability.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011147\xe2\x80\x9348_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011147\xe2\x80\x9348-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002230\xe2\x80\x9331_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002230\xe2\x80\x9331-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> He received further academic recognition, including five more honorary degrees,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011146_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011146-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Medal_of_the_Royal_Astronomical_Society" title="Gold Medal of the Royal Astronomical Society">Gold Medal of the Royal Astronomical Society</a> (1985),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xvi_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xvi-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Dirac_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Dirac Prize">Paul Dirac Medal</a> (1987)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011146_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011146-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> and, jointly with Penrose, the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Prize" title="Wolf Prize">Wolf Prize</a> (1988).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002279_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002279-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/1989_Birthday_Honours" title="1989 Birthday Honours">1989 Birthday Honours</a>, he was appointed a <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Companions_of_Honour" title="Order of the Companions of Honour">Companion of Honour</a> (CH).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011149_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011149-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> He reportedly declined a knighthood in the late 1990s in objection to the UK\'s science funding policy.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1990.E2.80.932000"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1990\xe2\x80\x932000">1990\xe2\x80\x932000</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gross_Witten_Hawking_TIFR_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Hawking outside, in his wheelchair, talking to David Gross and Edward Witten" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Gross_Witten_Hawking_TIFR_2001.jpg/250px-Gross_Witten_Hawking_TIFR_2001.jpg" width="250" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Gross_Witten_Hawking_TIFR_2001.jpg/375px-Gross_Witten_Hawking_TIFR_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Gross_Witten_Hawking_TIFR_2001.jpg/500px-Gross_Witten_Hawking_TIFR_2001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="593" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gross_Witten_Hawking_TIFR_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hawking with <a href="/wiki/String_theory" title="String theory">string theorists</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Gross" title="David Gross">David Gross</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Witten" title="Edward Witten">Edward Witten</a> at the 2001 Strings Conference, <a href="/wiki/TIFR" class="mw-redirect" title="TIFR">TIFR</a>, India</div></div></div>\n<p>Hawking pursued his work in physics: in 1993 he co-edited a book on <a href="/wiki/Euclidean_quantum_gravity" title="Euclidean quantum gravity">Euclidean quantum gravity</a> with Gary Gibbons and published a collected edition of his own articles on black holes and the Big Bang.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011180_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011180-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> In 1994, at Cambridge\'s <a href="/wiki/Newton_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Newton Institute">Newton Institute</a>, Hawking and Penrose delivered a series of six lectures that were published in 1996 as "The Nature of Space and Time".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011188_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011188-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, he conceded a 1991 public <a href="/wiki/Scientific_wager" title="Scientific wager">scientific wager</a> made with Kip Thorne and <a href="/wiki/John_Preskill" title="John Preskill">John Preskill</a> of <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">Caltech</a>. Hawking had bet that Penrose\'s proposal of a "cosmic censorship conjecture"&#160;&#8211;&#32;that there could be no "naked singularities" unclothed within a horizon&#160;&#8211;&#32;was correct.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011189\xe2\x80\x9390_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011189\xe2\x80\x9390-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> After discovering his concession might have been premature, a new and more refined wager was made. This one specified that such singularities would occur without extra conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011190_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011190-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The same year, Thorne, Hawking and Preskill made another bet, this time concerning the <a href="/wiki/Black_hole_information_paradox" title="Black hole information paradox">black hole information paradox</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-18_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-18-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-concedbet_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concedbet-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Thorne and Hawking argued that since general relativity made it impossible for black holes to radiate and lose information, the mass-energy and information carried by Hawking radiation must be "new", and not from inside the black hole <a href="/wiki/Event_horizon" title="Event horizon">event horizon</a>. Since this contradicted the quantum mechanics of microcausality, quantum mechanics theory would need to be rewritten. Preskill argued the opposite, that since quantum mechanics suggests that the information emitted by a black hole relates to information that fell in at an earlier time, the concept of black holes given by general relativity must be modified in some way.<sup id="cite_ref-presskill_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presskill-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking also maintained his public profile, including bringing science to a wider audience. A film version of <i>A Brief History of Time</i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Errol_Morris" title="Errol Morris">Errol Morris</a> and produced by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>, premiered in 1992. Hawking had wanted the film to be scientific rather than biographical, but he was persuaded otherwise. The film, while a critical success, was not widely released.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011168\xe2\x80\x9370_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011168\xe2\x80\x9370-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> A popular-level collection of essays, interviews, and talks titled <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Holes_and_Baby_Universes_and_Other_Essays" title="Black Holes and Baby Universes and Other Essays">Black Holes and Baby Universes and Other Essays</a></i> was published in 1993,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011178_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011178-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> and a six-part television series <i><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking%27s_Universe" title="Stephen Hawking&#39;s Universe">Stephen Hawking\'s Universe</a></i> and a companion book appeared in 1997. As Hawking insisted, this time the focus was entirely on science.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011189_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011189-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200597_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200597-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.932018"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000\xe2\x80\x932018">2000\xe2\x80\x932018</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Hawking_050506.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Stephen Hawking sitting in his wheelchair inside" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Stephen_Hawking_050506.jpg/170px-Stephen_Hawking_050506.jpg" width="170" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Stephen_Hawking_050506.jpg/255px-Stephen_Hawking_050506.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Stephen_Hawking_050506.jpg/340px-Stephen_Hawking_050506.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1606" data-file-height="2495" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Hawking_050506.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hawking at the <i lang="fr" title="French language text"><a href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_nationale_de_France" title="Biblioth\xc3\xa8que nationale de France">Biblioth\xc3\xa8que nationale de France</a></i> to inaugurate the Laboratory of Astronomy and Particles in Paris, and the French release of his work <i><a href="/wiki/God_Created_the_Integers" title="God Created the Integers">God Created the Integers</a></i>, 5 May 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>Hawking continued his writings for a popular audience, publishing <i><a href="/wiki/The_Universe_in_a_Nutshell" title="The Universe in a Nutshell">The Universe in a Nutshell</a></i> in 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011199\xe2\x80\x93200_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011199\xe2\x80\x93200-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Briefer_History_of_Time_(Hawking_and_Mlodinow_book)" title="A Briefer History of Time (Hawking and Mlodinow book)">A Briefer History of Time</a></i>, which he wrote in 2005 with <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Mlodinow" title="Leonard Mlodinow">Leonard Mlodinow</a> to update his earlier works with the aim of making them accessible to a wider audience, and <i><a href="/wiki/God_Created_the_Integers" title="God Created the Integers">God Created the Integers</a></i>, which appeared in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011222\xe2\x80\x9323_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011222\xe2\x80\x9323-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Along with <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Hertog" class="extiw" title="nl:Thomas Hertog">Thomas Hertog</a> at <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> and Jim Hartle, from 2006 on Hawking developed a theory of <span id="Top-down_cosmology"></span>"top-down cosmology", which says that the universe had not one unique initial state but many different ones, and therefore that it is inappropriate to formulate a theory that predicts the universe\'s current configuration from one particular initial state.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-23_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-23-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Top-down cosmology posits that the present "selects" the past from a superposition of many possible histories. In doing so, the theory suggests a possible resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Fine-tuned_universe" class="mw-redirect" title="Fine-tuned universe">fine-tuning question</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dt70_182-0"
