class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt70-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-24_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-24-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking continued to travel widely, including trips to Chile, <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a>, South Africa, Spain (to receive the <a href="/wiki/Fonseca_Prize" title="Fonseca Prize">Fonseca Prize</a> in 2008),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011233_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011233-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-29_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-29-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011239_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011239-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> and numerous trips to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011269_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011269-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> For practical reasons related to his disability, Hawking increasingly travelled by private jet, and by 2011 that had become his only mode of international travel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011197,269_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011197,269-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Weston_Library_Opening_by_John_Cairns_20.3.15-139.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Weston_Library_Opening_by_John_Cairns_20.3.15-139.jpg/220px-Weston_Library_Opening_by_John_Cairns_20.3.15-139.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Weston_Library_Opening_by_John_Cairns_20.3.15-139.jpg/330px-Weston_Library_Opening_by_John_Cairns_20.3.15-139.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Weston_Library_Opening_by_John_Cairns_20.3.15-139.jpg/440px-Weston_Library_Opening_by_John_Cairns_20.3.15-139.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2172" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Weston_Library_Opening_by_John_Cairns_20.3.15-139.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hawking with University of Oxford librarian <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ovenden" title="Richard Ovenden">Richard Ovenden</a> (left) and naturalist <a href="/wiki/David_Attenborough" title="David Attenborough">David Attenborough</a> (right) at the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Weston_Library" title="Weston Library">Weston Library</a>, Oxford, in March 2015. Ovenden awarded the <a href="/wiki/Bodley_Medal" title="Bodley Medal">Bodley Medal</a> to Hawking and Attenborough at the ceremony.</div></div></div>\n<p>By 2003, consensus among physicists was growing that Hawking was wrong about the loss of information in a black hole.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011216\xe2\x80\x9317_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011216\xe2\x80\x9317-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> In a 2004 lecture in Dublin, he conceded his 1997 bet with Preskill, but described his own, somewhat controversial solution to the information paradox problem, involving the possibility that black holes have more than one <a href="/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">topology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011217\xe2\x80\x9320_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011217\xe2\x80\x9320-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-presskill_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presskill-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In the 2005 paper he published on the subject, he argued that the information paradox was explained by examining all the alternative histories of universes, with the information loss in those with black holes being cancelled out by those without such loss.<sup id="cite_ref-concedbet_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-concedbet-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223\xe2\x80\x9324_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223\xe2\x80\x9324-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> In January 2014, he called the alleged loss of information in black holes his "biggest blunder".<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As part of another longstanding scientific dispute, Hawking had emphatically argued, and bet, that the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">Higgs boson</a> would never be found.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201195,_236_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201195,_236-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The particle was proposed to exist as part of the <a href="/wiki/Higgs_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Higgs field">Higgs field</a> theory by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Higgs" title="Peter Higgs">Peter Higgs</a> in 1964. Hawking and Higgs engaged in a heated and public debate over the matter in 2002 and again in 2008, with Higgs criticising Hawking\'s work and complaining that Hawking\'s "celebrity status gives him instant credibility that others do not have."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201194\xe2\x80\x9395,_236_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201194\xe2\x80\x9395,_236-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The particle was discovered in July 2012 at <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> following construction of the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a>. Hawking quickly conceded that he had lost his bet<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-42_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-42-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-43_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-43-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> and said that Higgs should win the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Physics" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize for Physics">Nobel Prize for Physics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-44_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-44-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> which he did in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Hawking_in_Stockholm,_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Stephen_Hawking_in_Stockholm%2C_2015.jpg/220px-Stephen_Hawking_in_Stockholm%2C_2015.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Stephen_Hawking_in_Stockholm%2C_2015.jpg/330px-Stephen_Hawking_in_Stockholm%2C_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Stephen_Hawking_in_Stockholm%2C_2015.jpg/440px-Stephen_Hawking_in_Stockholm%2C_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Hawking_in_Stockholm,_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hawking holding a public lecture at the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Waterfront" title="Stockholm Waterfront">Stockholm Waterfront</a> congress centre, 24 August 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2007, Hawking and his daughter <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Hawking" title="Lucy Hawking">Lucy</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/George%27s_Secret_Key_to_the_Universe" title="George&#39;s Secret Key to the Universe">George\'s Secret Key to the Universe</a></i>, a children\'s book designed to explain theoretical physics in an accessible fashion and featuring characters similar to those in the Hawking family.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011230\xe2\x80\x93231_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011230\xe2\x80\x93231-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The book was followed by <a href="/wiki/George%27s_Cosmic_Treasure_Hunt" title="George&#39;s Cosmic Treasure Hunt">sequels</a> in 2009, 2011, 2014 and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-books_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2002, following a UK-wide vote, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> included Hawking in their list of the <a href="/wiki/100_Greatest_Britons" title="100 Greatest Britons">100 Greatest Britons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> He was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Copley_Medal" title="Copley Medal">Copley Medal</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a> (2006),<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-45_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-45-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>, which is America\'s highest civilian honour (2009),<sup id="cite_ref-presidential_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presidential-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> and the Russian <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_Physics_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundamental Physics Prize">Special Fundamental Physics Prize</a> (2013).<sup id="cite_ref-FPP-Dec2012_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FPP-Dec2012-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several buildings have been named after him, including the Stephen W. Hawking Science Museum in <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">San Salvador</a>, El<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Salvador,<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-46_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-46-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> the Stephen Hawking Building in Cambridge,<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-47_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-47-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Perimeter_Institute_for_Theoretical_Physics#Stephen_Hawking_Centre_at_Perimeter_Institute" title="Perimeter Institute for Theoretical Physics">Stephen Hawking Centre</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Perimeter_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Perimeter Institute">Perimeter Institute</a> in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-48_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-48-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Appropriately, given Hawking\'s association with time, he unveiled the mechanical "Chronophage" (or time-eating) <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Clock" title="Corpus Clock">Corpus Clock</a> at <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_College_Cambridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Corpus Christi College Cambridge">Corpus Christi College, Cambridge</a> in September 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011237\xe2\x80\x9338_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011237\xe2\x80\x9338-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-49_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-49-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During his career, Hawking supervised 39 successful PhD students.<sup id="cite_ref-mathgene_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mathgene-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> One doctoral student did not successfully complete the PhD.<sup id="cite_ref-mathgene_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mathgene-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (August 2018)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> As required by Cambridge University regulations, Hawking retired as Lucasian Professor of Mathematics in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-lucasian_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lucasian-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-11_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-11-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Despite suggestions that he might leave the United Kingdom as a protest against public funding cuts to basic scientific research,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011238\xe2\x80\x9339_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011238\xe2\x80\x9339-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Hawking worked as director of research at the Cambridge University Department of Applied Mathematics and Theoretical Physics.<sup id="cite_ref-tel2012_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tel2012-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 June 2009, as a tongue-in-cheek test of his 1992 conjecture that travel into the past is effectively impossible, Hawking held a party open to all, complete with hors d\'oeuvres and iced champagne, but publicised the party only after it was over so that only time-travellers would know to attend; as expected, nobody showed up to the party.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 July 2015, Hawking helped launch <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Initiatives" title="Breakthrough Initiatives">Breakthrough Initiatives</a>, an effort to search for <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">extraterrestrial life</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AP-20150720_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP-20150720-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Hawking created <i>Stephen Hawking: Expedition New Earth</i>, a documentary on space colonisation, as a 2017 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow%27s_World" title="Tomorrow&#39;s World">Tomorrow\'s World</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2015, Hawking said that not all information is lost when something enters a black hole and there might be a possibility to retrieve information from a black hole according to his theory.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In July 2017, Hawking was awarded an Honorary Doctorate from <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking\'s final paper &#8211; <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007%2FJHEP04%282018%29147">A smooth exit from eternal inflation?</a></i> &#8211; was published in the <i><a href="/wiki/Journal_of_High_Energy_Physics" title="Journal of High Energy Physics">Journal of High Energy Physics</a></i> on 27 April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriages">Marriages</span></h3>\n<p>When Hawking was a graduate student at Cambridge, his relationship with <a href="/wiki/Jane_Hawking" title="Jane Hawking">Jane Wilde</a>, a friend of his sister whom he had met shortly before his late 1963 diagnosis with motor neurone disease, continued to develop. The couple became engaged in October 1964<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiv_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiv-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201137\xe2\x80\x9340_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201137\xe2\x80\x9340-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>&#160;&#8211;&#32;Hawking later said that the engagement gave him "something to live for"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201140_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201140-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>&#160;&#8211;&#32;and the two were married on 14 July 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201143\xe2\x80\x9344_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201143\xe2\x80\x9344-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During their first years of marriage, Jane lived in London during the week as she completed her degree, and they travelled to the United States several times for conferences and physics-related visits. The couple had difficulty finding housing that was within Hawking\'s walking distance to the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Applied_Mathematics_and_Theoretical_Physics" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Applied Mathematics and Theoretical Physics">Department of Applied Mathematics and Theoretical Physics</a> (DAMTP). Jane began a PhD programme, and a son, Robert, was born in May 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201145\xe2\x80\x9347_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201145\xe2\x80\x9347-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200292\xe2\x80\x9398_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200292\xe2\x80\x9398-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> A daughter, <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Hawking" title="Lucy Hawking">Lucy</a>, was born in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201165_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201165-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> A third child, Timothy, was born in April 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201192-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking rarely discussed his illness and physical challenges, even&#160;&#8211;&#32;in a precedent set during their courtship&#160;&#8211;&#32;with Jane.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201137\xe2\x80\x9339,_77_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201137\xe2\x80\x9339,_77-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> His disabilities meant that the responsibilities of home and family rested firmly on his wife\'s increasingly overwhelmed shoulders, leaving him more time to think about physics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201178_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201178-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Upon his appointment in 1974 to a year-long position at the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">California Institute of Technology</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena, California</a>, Jane proposed that a graduate or post-doctoral student live with them and help with his care. Hawking accepted, and <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Carr" title="Bernard Carr">Bernard Carr</a> travelled with them as the first of many students who fulfilled this role.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201182\xe2\x80\x9383_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201182\xe2\x80\x9383-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-black_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-black-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> The family spent a generally happy and stimulating year in Pasadena.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201183\xe2\x80\x9388_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201183\xe2\x80\x9388-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking returned to Cambridge in 1975 to a new home and a new job, as <a href="/wiki/Reader_(academic_rank)" title="Reader (academic rank)">reader</a>. <a href="/wiki/Don_Page_(physicist)" title="Don Page (physicist)">Don Page</a>, with whom Hawking had begun a close friendship at Caltech, arrived to work as the live-in graduate student assistant. With Page\'s help and that of a secretary, Jane\'s responsibilities were reduced so she could return to her thesis and her new interest in singing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201189\xe2\x80\x9390_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201189\xe2\x80\x9390-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By December 1977, Jane had met organist Jonathan Hellyer Jones when singing in a church choir. Hellyer Jones became close to the Hawking family, and by the mid-1980s, he and Jane had developed romantic feelings for each other.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201191_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201191-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiv,_79_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiv,_79-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHawking2007279\xe2\x80\x9380_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHawking2007279\xe2\x80\x9380-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> According to Jane, her husband was accepting of the situation, stating "he would not object so long as I continued to love him".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201191_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201191-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200579_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200579-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHawking2007285_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHawking2007285-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> Jane and Hellyer Jones determined not to break up the family, and their relationship remained platonic for a long period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201191\xe2\x80\x9392_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201191\xe2\x80\x9392-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the 1980s, Hawking\'s marriage had been strained for many years. Jane felt overwhelmed by the intrusion into their family life of the required nurses and assistants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011164\xe2\x80\x9365_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011164\xe2\x80\x9365-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> The impact of his celebrity was challenging for colleagues and family members, while the prospect of living up to a worldwide fairytale image was daunting for the couple.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011185_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011185-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dt70_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt70-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Hawking\'s views of religion also contrasted with her strong Christian faith and resulted in tension.<sup id="cite_ref-dt70_182-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt70-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201180\xe2\x80\x9381_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201180\xe2\x80\x9381-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-obs2004_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obs2004-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1980s, Hawking had grown close to one of his nurses, Elaine Mason, to the dismay of some colleagues, caregivers, and family members, who were disturbed by her strength of personality and protectiveness.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011145_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011145-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Hawking told Jane that he was leaving her for Mason,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011165_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011165-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> and departed the family home in February 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005x\xe2\x80\x93xix_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005x\xe2\x80\x93xix-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> After his divorce from Jane in 1995, Hawking married Mason in September,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011186\xe2\x80\x9387_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011186\xe2\x80\x9387-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005x\xe2\x80\x93xix_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005x\xe2\x80\x93xix-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> declaring, "It\'s wonderful&#160;&#8211;&#32;I have married the woman I love."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011187_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011187-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1999, Jane Hawking published a memoir, <i>Music to Move the Stars</i>, describing her marriage to Hawking and its breakdown. Its revelations caused a sensation in the media but, as was his usual practice regarding his personal life, Hawking made no public comment except to say that he did not read biographies about himself.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011187,_192_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011187,_192-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> After his second marriage, Hawking\'s family felt excluded and marginalised from his life.<sup id="cite_ref-obs2004_239-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obs2004-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sundaytimes_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaytimes-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> For a period of about five years in the early 2000s, his family and staff became increasingly worried that he was being physically abused.<sup id="cite_ref-sundaytimes_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaytimes-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011197,_225_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011197,_225-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Police investigations took place, but were closed as Hawking refused to make a complaint.<sup id="cite_ref-sundaytimes_245-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaytimes-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-21_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-21-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-22_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-22-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, Hawking and Mason quietly divorced,<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-25_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-25-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011225_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011225-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> and Hawking resumed closer relationships with Jane, his children, and his grandchildren.<sup id="cite_ref-dt70_182-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt70-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011225_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011225-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Reflecting this happier period, a revised version of Jane\'s book called <i>Travelling to Infinity: My Life with Stephen</i> appeared in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-sundaytimes_245-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaytimes-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> and was made into a film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Theory_of_Everything_(2014_film)" title="The Theory of Everything (2014 film)">The Theory of Everything</a></i>, in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disability">Disability</span></h3>\n<p>Hawking had a rare early-onset slow-progressing form of <a href="/wiki/Motor_neurone_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor neurone disease">motor neurone disease</a> (also known as <a href="/wiki/Amyotrophic_lateral_sclerosis" title="Amyotrophic lateral sclerosis">amyotrophic lateral sclerosis</a>, "<a href="/wiki/ALS" class="mw-redirect" title="ALS">ALS</a>", or <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a>\'s disease), that gradually paralysed him over the decades.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking had experienced increasing clumsiness during his final year at Oxford, including a fall on some stairs and difficulties when rowing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201132_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201132-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-6_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-6-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> The problems worsened, and his speech became slightly <a href="/wiki/Dysarthria" title="Dysarthria">slurred</a> and his family noticed the changes when he returned home for Christmas, and medical investigations were begun.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200259_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200259-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201134\xe2\x80\x9335_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201134\xe2\x80\x9335-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> The diagnosis of motor neurone disease came when Hawking was 21, in 1963. At the time, doctors gave him a life expectancy of two years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200518\xe2\x80\x9319_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200518\xe2\x80\x9319-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200259\xe2\x80\x9361_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin200259\xe2\x80\x9361-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the late 1960s, Hawking\'s physical abilities declined: he began to use crutches and could no longer give lectures regularly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201148\xe2\x80\x9349_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201148\xe2\x80\x9349-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> As he slowly lost the ability to write, he developed compensatory visual methods, including seeing equations in terms of geometry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201176\xe2\x80\x9377_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201176\xe2\x80\x9377-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002124\xe2\x80\x9325_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002124\xe2\x80\x9325-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> The physicist <a href="/wiki/Werner_Israel" title="Werner Israel">Werner Israel</a> later compared the achievements to <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a> composing an entire symphony in his head.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-8_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-8-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002124_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002124-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Hawking was fiercely independent and unwilling to accept help or make concessions for his disabilities. He preferred to be regarded as "a scientist first, popular science writer second, and, in all the ways that matter, a normal human being with the same desires, drives, dreams, and ambitions as the next person."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002viii_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002viii-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> His wife, <a href="/wiki/Jane_Hawking" title="Jane Hawking">Jane Hawking</a>, later noted: "Some people would call it determination, some obstinacy. I\'ve called it both at one time or another."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201148_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201148-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> He required much persuasion to accept the use of a wheelchair at the end of the 1960s,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002117_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002117-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> but ultimately became notorious for the wildness of his wheelchair driving.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011162_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011162-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> Hawking was a popular and witty colleague, but his illness, as well as his reputation for brashness, distanced him from some.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201148_264-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201148-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking\'s speech deteriorated, and by the late 1970s he could be understood by only his family and closest friends. To communicate with others, someone who knew him well would interpret his speech into intelligible speech.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201181\xe2\x80\x9382_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201181\xe2\x80\x9382-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Spurred by a dispute with the university over who would pay for the ramp needed for him to enter his workplace, Hawking and his wife campaigned for improved access and support for those with disabilities in Cambridge,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMialet2003450\xe2\x80\x9351_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMialet2003450\xe2\x80\x9351-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson201179,_149_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson201179,_149-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> including adapted student housing at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002273\xe2\x80\x9374_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002273\xe2\x80\x9374-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> In general, Hawking had ambivalent feelings about his role as a <a href="/wiki/Disability_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Disability rights">disability rights</a> champion: while wanting to help others, he also sought to detach himself from his illness and its challenges.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002193\xe2\x80\x9394_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002193\xe2\x80\x9394-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> His lack of engagement in this area led to some criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002194_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002194-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During a visit to <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">CERN</a> on the border of France and Switzerland in mid-1985, Hawking contracted <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>, which in his condition was life-threatening; he was so ill that Jane was asked if life support should be terminated. She refused, but the consequence was a <a href="/wiki/Tracheotomy" title="Tracheotomy">tracheotomy</a>, which required round-the-clock nursing care and the removal of what remained of his speech.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011135\xe2\x80\x9336_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011135\xe2\x80\x9336-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002232\xe2\x80\x9336_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002232\xe2\x80\x9336-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a> was ready to pay for a <a href="/wiki/Nursing_home" class="mw-redirect" title="Nursing home">nursing home</a>, but Jane was determined that he would live at home. The cost of the care was funded by an American foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011136\xe2\x80\x9337_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011136\xe2\x80\x9337-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002235\xe2\x80\x9336_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002235\xe2\x80\x9336-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Nurses were hired for the three shifts required to provide the round-the-clock support he required. One of those employed was Elaine Mason, who was to become Hawking\'s second wife.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011139_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011139-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For his communication, Hawking initially raised his eyebrows to choose <a href="/wiki/Partner-assisted_scanning" title="Partner-assisted scanning">letters on a spelling card</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011136_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011136-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> but in 1986 he received a computer program called the "Equalizer" from Walter Woltosz, CEO of Words Plus, who had developed an earlier version of the software to help his mother-in-law, who also suffered from ALS and had lost her ability to speak and write.<sup id="cite_ref-Medeiros_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medeiros-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> In a method he used for the rest of his life, Hawking could now simply press a switch to select phrases, words or letters from a bank of about 2,500\xe2\x80\x933,000 that were <a href="/wiki/Switch_access_scanning" title="Switch access scanning">scanned</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011137\xe2\x80\x9338_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011137\xe2\x80\x9338-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002236\xe2\x80\x9337_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002236\xe2\x80\x9337-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> The program was originally run on a desktop computer. Elaine Mason\'s husband, David, a computer engineer, adapted a small computer and attached it to his wheelchair.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011140_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011140-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> Released from the need to use somebody to interpret his speech, Hawking commented that "I can communicate better now than before I lost my voice."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011140\xe2\x80\x9341_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011140\xe2\x80\x9341-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> The voice he used had an American accent and is no longer produced.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011138_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011138-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-15_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-15-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Despite the later availability of other voices, Hawking retained this original voice, saying that he preferred it and identified with it.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-16_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-16-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> Originally, Hawking activated a switch using his hand and could produce up to <a href="/wiki/Typing#Alphanumeric_entry" title="Typing">15 words a minute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011137_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011137-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Lectures were prepared in advance and were sent to the <a href="/wiki/Speech_synthesis" title="Speech synthesis">speech synthesizer</a> in short sections to be delivered.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011138_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011138-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking gradually lost the use of his hand, and in 2005 he began to control his communication device with movements of his cheek muscles,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011224_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011224-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tech_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tech-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hacked_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hacked-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> with a rate of about one word per minute.<sup id="cite_ref-tech_288-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tech-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> With this decline there was a risk of his developing <a href="/wiki/Locked-in_syndrome" title="Locked-in syndrome">locked-in syndrome</a>, so Hawking collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> researchers on systems that could translate his <a href="/wiki/Neural_oscillation" title="Neural oscillation">brain patterns</a> or facial expressions into switch activations. After several prototypes that did not perform as planned, they settled on an adaptive word predictor made by the London-based startup <a href="/wiki/SwiftKey" title="SwiftKey">SwiftKey</a>, which used a system similar to his original technology. Hawking had an easier time adapting to the new system, which was further developed after inputting large amounts of Hawking\'s papers and other written materials and uses predictive software similar to other smartphone keyboards.<sup id="cite_ref-hacked_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hacked-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Medeiros_279-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medeiros-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dt70_182-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt70-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-start_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-start-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> By 2009 he could no longer drive his wheelchair independently, but the same people who created his new typing mechanics were working on a method to drive his chair using movements made by his chin. This proved difficult, since Hawking could not move his neck, and trials showed that while he could indeed drive the chair, the movement was sporadic and jumpy.<sup id="cite_ref-Medeiros_279-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medeiros-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011240_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011240-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> Near the end of his life, Hawking experienced increased breathing difficulties, often resulting in his requiring the usage of a <a href="/wiki/Ventilator" class="mw-redirect" title="Ventilator">ventilator</a>, and being regularly hospitalised.<sup id="cite_ref-dt70_182-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt70-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disability_outreach">Disability outreach</span></h3>\n<p>Starting in the 1990s, Hawking accepted the mantle of role model for disabled people, lecturing and participating in fundraising activities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011164,_178_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011164,_178-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> At the turn of the century, he and eleven other luminaries signed the <i>Charter for the Third Millennium on Disability</i>, which called on governments to prevent disability and protect the rights of the disabled.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-19_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-19-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011196_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011196-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> In 1999, Hawking was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Lilienfeld_Prize" title="Lilienfeld Prize">Julius Edgar Lilienfeld Prize</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Physical_Society" title="American Physical Society">American Physical Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-20_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-20-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2012, Hawking narrated the "Enlightenment" segment of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Paralympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Paralympics opening ceremony">2012 Summer Paralympics opening ceremony</a> in London.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-54_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-54-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, the biographical documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/Hawking_(2013_film)" title="Hawking (2013 film)">Hawking</a></i>, in which Hawking himself is featured, was released.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20130913_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130913-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> In September 2013, he expressed support for the legalisation of <a href="/wiki/Assisted_suicide" title="Assisted suicide">assisted suicide</a> for the terminally ill.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-55_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-55-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> In August 2014, Hawking accepted the <a href="/wiki/Ice_Bucket_Challenge" title="Ice Bucket Challenge">Ice Bucket Challenge</a> to promote ALS/MND awareness and raise contributions for research. As he had pneumonia in 2013, he was advised not to have ice poured over him, but his children volunteered to accept the challenge on his behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-57_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-57-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans_for_a_trip_to_space">Plans for a trip to space</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Physicist_Stephen_Hawking_in_Zero_Gravity_NASA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Hawking, without his wheelchair, floating weightless in the air inside a plane" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Physicist_Stephen_Hawking_in_Zero_Gravity_NASA.jpg/250px-Physicist_Stephen_Hawking_in_Zero_Gravity_NASA.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Physicist_Stephen_Hawking_in_Zero_Gravity_NASA.jpg/375px-Physicist_Stephen_Hawking_in_Zero_Gravity_NASA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Physicist_Stephen_Hawking_in_Zero_Gravity_NASA.jpg/500px-Physicist_Stephen_Hawking_in_Zero_Gravity_NASA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3990" data-file-height="2660" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Physicist_Stephen_Hawking_in_Zero_Gravity_NASA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hawking taking a zero-gravity flight in a <a href="/wiki/Reduced-gravity_aircraft" title="Reduced-gravity aircraft">reduced-gravity aircraft</a>, 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>In late 2006, Hawking revealed in a BBC interview that one of his greatest unfulfilled desires was to travel to space;<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-32_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-32-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> on hearing this, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a> offered a free flight into space with <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Galactic" title="Virgin Galactic">Virgin Galactic</a>, which Hawking immediately accepted. Besides personal ambition, he was motivated by the desire to increase public interest in spaceflight and to show the potential of people with disabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt2007_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt2007-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> On 26 April 2007, Hawking flew aboard a <a href="/wiki/Reduced-gravity_aircraft" title="Reduced-gravity aircraft">specially-modified</a> Boeing 727\xe2\x80\x93200 jet operated by <a href="/wiki/Zero_Gravity_Corporation" title="Zero Gravity Corporation">Zero-G Corp</a> off the coast of Florida to experience weightlessness.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011232\xe2\x80\x9333_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011232\xe2\x80\x9333-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> Fears the manoeuvres would cause him undue discomfort proved groundless, and the flight was extended to eight parabolic arcs.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-32_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-32-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> It was described as a successful test to see if he could withstand the g-forces involved in space flight.<sup id="cite_ref-Leonard2007_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leonard2007-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> At the time, the date of Hawking\'s trip to space was projected to be as early as 2009, but commercial flights to space did not commence before his death.<sup id="cite_ref-Dean2018_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dean2018-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span></h2>\n<p>Hawking died at his home in <a href="/wiki/Cambridge" title="Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, England, early in the morning of 14 March 2018, at the age of 76.<sup id="cite_ref-ReesNatureObituary_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReesNatureObituary-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT=20180314_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT=20180314-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian.Death_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian.Death-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> His family stated that he "died peacefully".<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> He was eulogised by figures in science, entertainment, politics, and other areas.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20180314do_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20180314do-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20180314lm_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20180314lm-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC-Memorials_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-Memorials-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gonville_and_Caius_College,_Cambridge" title="Gonville and Caius College, Cambridge">Gonville and Caius College</a> flag flew at <a href="/wiki/Half-mast" title="Half-mast">half-mast</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Book_of_condolence" class="mw-redirect" title="Book of condolence">book of condolences</a> was signed by students and visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20180314db2_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20180314db2-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> A tribute was made to Hawking in the closing speech by <a href="/wiki/International_Paralympic_Committee" title="International Paralympic Committee">IPC</a> President <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Parsons_(sports_administrator)" title="Andrew Parsons (sports administrator)">Andrew Parsons</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Paralympics_closing_ceremony" title="2018 Winter Paralympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Paralympics" title="2018 Winter Paralympics">2018 Paralympic Winter Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pyeongchang_County" title="Pyeongchang County">Pyeongchang</a>, South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> Hawking\'s final broadcast interview, about the detection of <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_waves" class="mw-redirect" title="Gravitational waves">gravitational waves</a> resulting from the <a href="/wiki/GW170817" title="GW170817">collision of two neutron stars</a>, occurred in October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-20180326_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-20180326-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> His final words to the world appeared posthumously, in April 2018, in the form of a <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Channel" title="Smithsonian Channel">Smithsonian TV Channel</a> documentary entitled, <i>Leaving Earth: Or How to Colonize a Planet</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MT-20180324_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MT-20180324-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SPC-20180313_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPC-20180313-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> His final research study, entitled <i>A smooth exit from eternal inflation?</i>, about the <a href="/wiki/Physical_cosmology" title="Physical cosmology">origin of the universe</a>, was published in the <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_High_Energy_Physics" title="Journal of High Energy Physics">Journal of High Energy Physics</a> in May 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-PHYS-20180502_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PHYS-20180502-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JHEP-20180420_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JHEP-20180420-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JHEP-20180420pdf_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JHEP-20180420pdf-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking was born on the 300th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo\'s</a> death and died on the 139th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Einstein\'s</a> birth.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200551_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200551-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> His private funeral took place at 2&#160;pm on the afternoon of 31 March 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-CNWS-20180331_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNWS-20180331-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> at <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St_Mary_the_Great,_Cambridge" title="Church of St Mary the Great, Cambridge">Great St Mary\'s Church</a>, Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-CNWS-20180331_324-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNWS-20180331-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20180331_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20180331-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> Guests at the funeral included <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Redmayne" title="Eddie Redmayne">Eddie Redmayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Felicity_Jones" title="Felicity Jones">Felicity Jones</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> guitarist and astrophysicist <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-20180331_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-20180331-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> Following the cremation a service of thanksgiving was held at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> on 15 June 2018, after which his ashes were interred in the Abbey\'s <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">nave</a>, alongside the grave of Sir <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a> and close to that of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HawkingWestminster_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HawkingWestminster-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC-20180331_326-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-20180331-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the service, readings and tributes were made by <a href="/wiki/Benedict_Cumberbatch" title="Benedict Cumberbatch">Benedict Cumberbatch</a>, who played Hawking in a <a href="/wiki/Hawking_(2004_film)" title="Hawking (2004 film)">BBC television film</a>, astronaut <a href="/wiki/Tim_Peake" title="Tim Peake">Tim Peake</a>, Astronomer <a href="/wiki/Martin_Rees" title="Martin Rees">Royal Martin Rees,</a> and Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Kip_Thorne" title="Kip Thorne">Kip Thorne</a>.\n</p><p>Hawking\'s words, set to music by Greek composer <a href="/wiki/Vangelis" title="Vangelis">Vangelis</a>, are to be beamed into space from a European space agency satellite dish in Spain with the aim of reaching the nearest black hole, 1A 0620-00. \n</p><p>Inscribed on his memorial stone are the words "Here lies what was mortal of Stephen Hawking 1942 - 2018" and his most famed equation.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He directed, at least fifteen years before his death, that the <a href="/wiki/Bekenstein%E2%80%93Hawking_entropy_equation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bekenstein\xe2\x80\x93Hawking entropy equation">Bekenstein\xe2\x80\x93Hawking entropy equation</a> be his <a href="/wiki/Epitaph" title="Epitaph">epitaph</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Highfield2002_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highfield2002-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_views">Personal views</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_of_humanity">Future of humanity</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_speaks_to_Stephen_Hawking_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of Barack Obama talking to Stephen Hawking in the White House" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Barack_Obama_speaks_to_Stephen_Hawking_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Barack_Obama_speaks_to_Stephen_Hawking_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Barack_Obama_speaks_to_Stephen_Hawking_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Barack_Obama_speaks_to_Stephen_Hawking_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Barack_Obama_speaks_to_Stephen_Hawking_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Barack_Obama_speaks_to_Stephen_Hawking_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1876" data-file-height="2333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_speaks_to_Stephen_Hawking_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> talks with Hawking in the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> before a ceremony presenting him with the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a> on 12 August 2009.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2006, Hawking posed an open question on the Internet: "In a world that is in chaos politically, socially and environmentally, how can the human race sustain another 100 years?", later clarifying: "I don\'t know the answer. That is why I asked the question, to get people to think about it, and to be aware of the dangers we now face."<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking expressed concern that life on Earth is at risk from a sudden nuclear war, a genetically engineered <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">virus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>, or other dangers humans have not yet thought of.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt2007_301-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt2007-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_planet_Earth_337-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_planet_Earth-337">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> Such a planet-wide disaster need not result in human extinction if the human race were to be able to colonise additional planets before the disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_planet_Earth_337-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_planet_Earth-337">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> Hawking viewed spaceflight and the colonisation of space as necessary for the future of humanity.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt2007_301-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt2007-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-31_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-31-338">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking stated that, given the vastness of the universe, <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">aliens</a> likely exist, but that contact with them should be avoided.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-30_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-30-339">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alien_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alien-340">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> He warned that aliens might pillage Earth for resources. In 2010 he said, "If aliens visit us, the outcome would be much as when Columbus landed in America, which didn\'t turn out well for the Native Americans."<sup id="cite_ref-alien_340-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alien-340">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking warned that <a href="/wiki/Superintelligent" class="mw-redirect" title="Superintelligent">superintelligent</a> <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> could be pivotal in steering humanity\'s fate, stating that "the potential benefits are huge... Success in creating AI would be the biggest event in human history. It might also be the last, unless we learn how to avoid the risks."<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> However, he argued that we should be more <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_capitalism" title="Criticism of capitalism">frightened of capitalism</a> exacerbating <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">economic inequality</a> than robots.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking argued that <a href="/wiki/Computer_virus" title="Computer virus">computer viruses</a> should be considered a new form of life, and stated that "maybe it says something about human nature, that the only form of life we have created so far is purely destructive. Talk about creating life in our own image."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011179_344-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011179-344">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_vs._philosophy">Science vs. philosophy</span></h3>\n<p>At Google\'s Zeitgeist Conference in 2011, Hawking said that "philosophy is dead". He believed that philosophers "have not kept up with modern developments in science" and that scientists "have become the bearers of the torch of discovery in our quest for knowledge". He said that <a href="/wiki/List_of_unsolved_problems_in_philosophy" title="List of unsolved problems in philosophy">philosophical problems</a> can be answered by science, particularly new scientific theories which "lead us to a new and very different picture of the universe and our place in it".<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-53_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-53-345">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion_and_atheism">Religion and atheism</span></h3>\n<p>Hawking was an <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a><sup id="cite_ref-atheist_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atheist-346">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> and believed that "the universe is governed by the laws of science". He stated: "There is a fundamental difference between religion, which is based on authority, [and] science, which is based on observation and reason. Science will win because it works."<sup id="cite_ref-Hollowverse_347-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollowverse-347">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> In an interview published in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, Hawking regarded "the brain as a computer which will stop working when its components fail", and the concept of an <a href="/wiki/Afterlife" title="Afterlife">afterlife</a> as a "fairy story for people afraid of the dark".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT=20180314_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT=20180314-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sample_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sample-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, narrating the first episode of the American television series <i><a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(TV_series)" title="Curiosity (TV series)">Curiosity</a></i> on the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Channel" title="Discovery Channel">Discovery Channel</a>, Hawking declared:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We are each free to believe what we want and it is my view that the simplest explanation is there is no God. No one created the universe and no one directs our fate. This leads me to a profound realisation. There is probably no heaven, and no afterlife either. We have this one life to appreciate the grand design of the universe, and for that, I am extremely grateful.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-50_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-50-348">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-51_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-51-349">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>In September 2014, he joined the <a href="/wiki/Starmus_Festival" title="Starmus Festival">Starmus Festival</a> as keynote speaker and declared himself an atheist.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-52_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-52-350">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Spain)" title="El Mundo (Spain)">El Mundo</a></i>, he said:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Before we understand science, it is natural to believe that God created the universe. But now science offers a more convincing explanation. What I meant by \'we would know the mind of God\' is, we would know everything that God would know, if there were a God, which there isn\'t. I\'m an atheist.<sup id="cite_ref-atheist_346-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atheist-346">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>\n<p>Hawking was a longstanding <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a> supporter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002195_351-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002195-351">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223-352">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> He recorded a tribute for the 2000 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011195_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011195-353">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup> called the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a> a "<a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crime</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223_352-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223-352">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-34_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-34-354">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup> supported the <a href="/wiki/Academic_boycott_of_Israel" title="Academic boycott of Israel">academic boycott of Israel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-35_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-35-355">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT-20130508_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20130508-356">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> campaigned for <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_disarmament" title="Nuclear disarmament">nuclear disarmament</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002195_351-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhiteGribbin2002195-351">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223_352-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223-352">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> and supported <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell" title="Stem cell">stem cell</a> research,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223_352-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011223-352">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-37_357-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-37-357">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011242_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011242-358">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> and action to prevent <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ind2007_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ind2007-359">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> In August 2014, Hawking was one of 200 public figures who were signatories to a letter to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> expressing their hope that Scotland would vote to remain part of the United Kingdom in September\'s <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">referendum on that issue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-56_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-56-360">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup> Hawking believed a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_withdrawal_from_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom withdrawal from the European Union">United Kingdom withdrawal from the European Union</a> (Brexit) would damage the UK\'s contribution to science as modern research needs international collaboration, and that free movement of people in Europe encourages the spread of ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> Hawking was disappointed by Brexit and warned against envy and isolationism.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking was greatly concerned over health care, and maintained that without the UK <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a>, he could not have survived into his 70s.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20/8/2017_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20/8/2017-363">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> He stated, "I have received excellent medical attention in Britain, and I felt it was important to set the record straight. I believe in <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a>. And I am not afraid to say so."<sup id="cite_ref-Hollowverse_347-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollowverse-347">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking feared privatisation. He stated, "The more profit is extracted from the system, the more private monopolies grow and the more expensive healthcare becomes. The NHS must be preserved from commercial interests and protected from those who want to privatise it."<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> Hawking alleged ministers damaged the NHS, he blamed the Conservatives for cutting funding, weakening the NHS by privatisation, lowering staff morale through holding pay back and reducing social care.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> Hawking accused <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Hunt" title="Jeremy Hunt">Jeremy Hunt</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cherry_picking" title="Cherry picking">cherry picking</a> evidence which Hawking maintained debased science.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20/8/2017_363-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20/8/2017-363">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> Hawking also stated, "There is overwhelming evidence that NHS funding and the numbers of doctors and nurses are inadequate, and it is getting worse."<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2017, Hawking endorsed the Labour Party in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">2017 UK general election</a>, citing the Conservatives\' proposed cuts to the NHS. But he was also critical of Labour leader <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>, expressing scepticism over whether the party could win a general election under him.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking feared <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>\'s policies on global warming could endanger the planet and make global warming irreversible. He said, "Climate change is one of the great dangers we face, and it\'s one we can prevent if we act now. By denying the evidence for climate change, and pulling out of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a>, Donald Trump will cause avoidable environmental damage to our beautiful planet, endangering the natural world, for us and our children."<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> Hawking further stated that this could lead Earth "to become like Venus, with a temperature of two hundred and fifty degrees, and raining sulphuric acid".<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearances_in_popular_media">Appearances in popular media</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking_in_popular_culture" title="Stephen Hawking in popular culture">Stephen Hawking in popular culture</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot;
