data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;574960&quot; data-framerate=&quot;29.97&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:Stephen Hawking at the White House with President Clinton.webm" style="width:220px;height:161px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Stephen_Hawking_at_the_White_House_with_President_Clinton.webm/220px--Stephen_Hawking_at_the_White_House_with_President_Clinton.webm.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cf/Stephen_Hawking_at_the_White_House_with_President_Clinton.webm" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_Hawking_at_the_White_House_with_President_Clinton.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hawking at the White House with <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">President Clinton</a> on 5 March 1998</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1988, Stephen Hawking, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke" title="Arthur C. Clarke">Arthur C. Clarke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">Carl Sagan</a> were interviewed in <i><a href="/wiki/God,_the_Universe_and_Everything_Else" title="God, the Universe and Everything Else">God, the Universe and Everything Else</a></i>. They discussed the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang_theory" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Bang theory">Big Bang theory</a>, God and the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">extraterrestrial life</a>.\n</p><p>At the release party for the home video version of the <i>A Brief History of Time</i>, <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Nimoy" title="Leonard Nimoy">Leonard Nimoy</a>, who had played <a href="/wiki/Spock" title="Spock">Spock</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">Star Trek</a></i>, learned that Hawking was interested in appearing on the show. Nimoy made the necessary contact, and Hawking played a holographic simulation of himself in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></i> in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011177\xe2\x80\x9378_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011177\xe2\x80\x9378-370">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen200593\xe2\x80\x9394_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen200593\xe2\x80\x9394-371">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOkudaOkuda1999380_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOkudaOkuda1999380-372">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> The same year, his synthesizer voice was recorded for the <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Keep_Talking" title="Keep Talking">Keep Talking</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiii,_94_373-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarsen2005xiii,_94-373">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011178_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011178-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> and in 1999 for an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011192_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011192-374">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> Hawking appeared in documentaries titled <i>The Real Stephen Hawking</i> (2001),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011196_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011196-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> <i>Stephen Hawking: Profile</i> (2002)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011221_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011221-375">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hawking_(2013_film)" title="Hawking (2013 film)">Hawking</a></i> (2013), and the documentary series <i>Stephen Hawking, Master of the Universe</i> (2008).<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-26_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-26-376">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> Hawking also guest-starred in <i><a href="/wiki/Futurama" title="Futurama">Futurama</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-dt70_182-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dt70-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Big_Bang_Theory" title="The Big Bang Theory">The Big Bang Theory</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-bbt_377-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-bbt-377">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking allowed the use of his copyrighted voice<sup id="cite_ref-Mialet_2012_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mialet_2012-378">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Edgar_2014_379-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edgar_2014-379">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup> in the biographical 2014 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Theory_of_Everything_(2014_film)" title="The Theory of Everything (2014 film)">The Theory of Everything</a></i>, in which he was portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Redmayne" title="Eddie Redmayne">Eddie Redmayne</a> in an Academy Award-winning role.<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> Hawking was featured at the <i><a href="/wiki/Monty_Python_Live_(Mostly)" title="Monty Python Live (Mostly)">Monty Python Live (Mostly)</a></i> in 2014. He was shown to sing an extended version of the <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_Song" title="Galaxy Song">Galaxy Song</a>, after running down <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cox_(physicist)" title="Brian Cox (physicist)">Brian Cox</a> with his wheelchair, in a pre-recorded video.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking used his fame to advertise products, including a wheelchair,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011196_294-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFerguson2011196-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NS%26I" class="mw-redirect" title="NS&amp;I">National Savings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-38_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-38-383">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/British_Telecom" class="mw-redirect" title="British Telecom">British Telecom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Specsavers" title="Specsavers">Specsavers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egg_Banking" title="Egg Banking">Egg Banking</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-39_384-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-39-384">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Go_Compare" class="mw-redirect" title="Go Compare">Go Compare</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-40_385-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-40-385">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup> In 2015 he applied to trademark his name.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Broadcast in March 2018 just a week or two before his death, Hawking was the voice of The Book Mark II on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hitchhiker%27s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy" title="The Hitchhiker&#39;s Guide to the Galaxy">The Hitchhiker\'s Guide to the Galaxy</a></i> radio series, and he was the guest of <a href="/wiki/Neil_deGrasse_Tyson" title="Neil deGrasse Tyson">Neil deGrasse Tyson</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/StarTalk_(2015_TV_series)" title="StarTalk (2015 TV series)">StarTalk</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honours">Awards and honours</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_hawking_and_lucy_hawking_nasa_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photograph of Hawking and his daughter Lucy on-stage at a presentation" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Stephen_hawking_and_lucy_hawking_nasa_2008.jpg/250px-Stephen_hawking_and_lucy_hawking_nasa_2008.jpg" width="250" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Stephen_hawking_and_lucy_hawking_nasa_2008.jpg/375px-Stephen_hawking_and_lucy_hawking_nasa_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Stephen_hawking_and_lucy_hawking_nasa_2008.jpg/500px-Stephen_hawking_and_lucy_hawking_nasa_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3460" data-file-height="2376" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen_hawking_and_lucy_hawking_nasa_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stephen Hawking being presented by his daughter <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Hawking" title="Lucy Hawking">Lucy Hawking</a> at the lecture he gave for <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>\'s 50th anniversary</div></div></div>\n<p>Hawking received numerous awards and honours. Already early in the list, in 1974 he was elected a Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a> (FRS). At that time, his nomination read:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Hawking has made major contributions to the field of general relativity. These derive from a deep understanding of what is relevant to physics and astronomy, and especially from a mastery of wholly new mathematical techniques. Following the pioneering work of Penrose he established, partly alone and partly in collaboration with Penrose, a series of successively stronger theorems establishing the fundamental result that all realistic cosmological models must possess singularities. Using similar techniques, Hawking has proved the basic theorems on the laws governing black holes: that stationary solutions of Einstein\'s equations with smooth event horizons must necessarily be axisymmetric; and that in the evolution and interaction of black holes, the total surface area of the event horizons must increase. In collaboration with G. Ellis, Hawking is the author of an impressive and original treatise on "Space-time in the Large".\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>The citation continues, "Other important work by Hawking relates to the interpretation of cosmological observations and to the design of gravitational wave detectors."<sup id="cite_ref-royal_388-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-royal-388">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hawking received the 2015 <a href="/wiki/BBVA_Foundation_Frontiers_of_Knowledge_Award" title="BBVA Foundation Frontiers of Knowledge Award">BBVA Foundation Frontiers of Knowledge Award</a> in Basic Sciences shared with <a href="/wiki/Viatcheslav_Mukhanov" title="Viatcheslav Mukhanov">Viatcheslav Mukhanov</a> for discovering that the galaxies were formed from quantum fluctuations in the early Universe. At the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Pride_of_Britain_Awards" title="Pride of Britain Awards">Pride of Britain Awards</a>, Hawking received the lifetime achievement award "for his contribution to science and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British culture</a>". After receiving the award from Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>, Hawking humorously requested that she not seek his help with <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stephen_Hawking_Medal_for_Science_Communication">Stephen Hawking Medal for Science Communication</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking_Medal_for_Science_Communication" title="Stephen Hawking Medal for Science Communication">Stephen Hawking Medal for Science Communication</a></div>\n<p>Hawking was a member of the Advisory Board of the <a href="/wiki/Starmus_Festival" title="Starmus Festival">Starmus Festival</a>, and had a major role in acknowledging and promoting science communication. The <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking_Medal_for_Science_Communication" title="Stephen Hawking Medal for Science Communication">Stephen Hawking Medal for Science Communication</a> is an annual award initiated in 2016 to honour members of the arts community for contributions that help build awareness of science.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup> Recipients receive a medal bearing a portrait of Stephen Hawking by <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Leonov" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexei Leonov">Alexei Leonov</a>, and the other side represents an image of Leonov himself performing his famous space walk and the iconic "<a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">Red Special</a>", <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a>\'s guitar.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Starmus_Festival#2016_Starmus_Festival,_&quot;Starmus_III&quot;" title="Starmus Festival">Starmus III Festival</a> in 2016 was a tribute to Stephen Hawking and the book of all Starmus III lectures, "Beyond the Horizon", was also dedicated to him.  The first recipients of the medals, which were awarded at the festival, were chosen by Hawking himself.  They were composer <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a>, physicist <a href="/wiki/Jim_Al-Khalili" title="Jim Al-Khalili">Jim Al-Khalili</a>, and the science documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Particle_Fever" title="Particle Fever">Particle Fever</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Black_Hole_discovery_dedication">Black Hole discovery dedication</span></h3>\n<p>In March 2018, it was announced that two Russian astronomers who discovered GRB180316A, a newborn black hole in the <a href="/wiki/Ophiuchus" title="Ophiuchus">Ophiuchus</a> constellation on 16 March 2018, had dedicated their find to Stephen Hawking, having discovered it two days after his death.<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span href="/wiki/Reduced_Planck_Constant" class="mw-redirect" title="Reduced Planck Constant">divided by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle 2\\pi }">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mn>2</mn>\n        <mi>&#x03C0;<!-- \xcf\x80 --></mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 2\\pi }</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/73efd1f6493490b058097060a572606d2c550a06" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.494ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="2\\pi "/></span></a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle c}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>c</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle c}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="c"/></span> is Einstein\'s <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">speed of light</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle G}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>G</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle G}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f5f3c8921a3b352de45446a6789b104458c9f90b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.827ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="G"/></span> is Newton\'s <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_constant" title="Gravitational constant">gravitational constant</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle M}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>M</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle M}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f82cade9898ced02fdd08712e5f0c0151758a0dd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.442ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="M"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">mass</a> of the black hole, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle k}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>k</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle k}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3c9a2c7b599b37105512c5d570edc034056dd40" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.211ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="k"/></span> is <a href="/wiki/Boltzmann%27s_constant" class="mw-redirect" title="Boltzmann&#39;s constant">Boltzmann\'s constant</a>. This relationship between concepts from the disparate fields of <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">quantum mechanics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamics" title="Thermodynamics">thermodynamics</a> implies the existence of deep connections between them and may presage their <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_everything" title="Theory of everything">unification</a>. It is inscribed on Hawking\'s memorial stone.<sup id="cite_ref-Bever2018_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bever2018-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup><br /><br />\n\nThe equation\'s most fundamental implication can be obtained as follows. According to thermodynamics, this temperature is associated with an <a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">entropy</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle S}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>S</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span>, such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle T=Mc^{2}/2S,}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>T</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi>M</mi>\n        <msup>\n          <mi>c</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msup>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <mn>2</mn>\n        <mi>S</mi>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T=Mc^{2}/2S,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1df0f52b758651f6c4c9a928470321778aadc040" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.709ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle T=Mc^{2}/2S,}"/></span> where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle Mc^{2}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>M</mi>\n        <msup>\n          <mi>c</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msup>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle Mc^{2}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7f1e81d5aacf191d5515d34e8c9872e0348cc539" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.503ex; height:2.676ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle Mc^{2}}"/></span> is the energy of a (nonspinning) black hole as expressed with <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass\xe2\x80\x93energy equivalence">Einstein\'s formula</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Walecka2007_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walecka2007-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> Combining equations then gives:\n\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle S={\\frac {4\\pi GM^{2}k}{\\hbar c}}.}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>S</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <mn>4</mn>\n              <mi>&#x03C0;<!-- \xcf\x80 --></mi>\n              <mi>G</mi>\n              <msup>\n                <mi>M</mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mn>2</mn>\n                </mrow>\n              </msup>\n              <mi>k</mi>\n            </mrow>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi class="MJX-variant">&#x210F;<!-- \xe2\x84\x8f --></mi>\n              <mi>c</mi>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S={\\frac {4\\pi GM^{2}k}{\\hbar c}}.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/66476fa38886d38b42423d5bf71e77f5ae4700f0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:15.166ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle S={\\frac {4\\pi GM^{2}k}{\\hbar c}}.}"/></span></dd></dl>\n\nNow, the <a href="/wiki/Schwarzschild_radius" title="Schwarzschild radius">radius of a nonspinning black hole</a> is given by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle r={\\frac {2GM}{c^{2}}},}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>r</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <mn>2</mn>\n              <mi>G</mi>\n              <mi>M</mi>\n            </mrow>\n            <msup>\n              <mi>c</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>2</mn>\n              </mrow>\n            </msup>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r={\\frac {2GM}{c^{2}}},}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6657e1ffb078b8f55a3120e9d6dd856765e9cc1f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:11.061ex; height:5.676ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle r={\\frac {2GM}{c^{2}}},}"/></span> and since its <a href="/wiki/Surface_area_of_a_sphere" class="mw-redirect" title="Surface area of a sphere">surface area</a> is just <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle A=4\\pi r^{2},}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>A</mi>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mn>4</mn>\n        <mi>&#x03C0;<!-- \xcf\x80 --></mi>\n        <msup>\n          <mi>r</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>2</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msup>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle A=4\\pi r^{2},}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ba1cbdbb8a22c7db3b3f01dad4ea19f8dfcd502b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:10.086ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle A=4\\pi r^{2},}"/></span> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle S}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>S</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span> can be expressed in terms of surface area as:\n\n<sup id="cite_ref-Highfield2002_329-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highfield2002-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Griffin2018_333-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Griffin2018-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup>\n\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle S_{\\text{BH}}={\\frac {kc^{3}}{4\\hbar G}}A,}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>S</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mtext>BH</mtext>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mrow>\n              <mi>k</mi>\n              <msup>\n                <mi>c</mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                  <mn>3</mn>\n                </mrow>\n              </msup>\n            </mrow>\n            <mrow>\n              <mn>4</mn>\n              <mi class="MJX-variant">&#x210F;<!-- \xe2\x84\x8f --></mi>\n              <mi>G</mi>\n            </mrow>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mi>A</mi>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S_{\\text{BH}}={\\frac {kc^{3}}{4\\hbar G}}A,}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/18ab61342a5df6da0a528acf9c4a2036b6fbfd4f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:14.673ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle S_{\\text{BH}}={\\frac {kc^{3}}{4\\hbar G}}A,}"/></span></dd></dl>\n\nwhere the subscript BH stands for either "black hole" or "Bekenstein\xe2\x80\x93Hawking". This can be expressed more simply as a proportionality between two <a href="/wiki/Dimensionless" class="mw-redirect" title="Dimensionless">dimensionless</a> ratios:\n\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {S_{\\text{BH}}}{k}}={\\frac {1}{4}}{\\frac {A}{A_{\\text{P}}}},}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <msub>\n              <mi>S</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mtext>BH</mtext>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n            <mi>k</mi>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mn>1</mn>\n            <mn>4</mn>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mi>A</mi>\n            <msub>\n              <mi>A</mi>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mtext>P</mtext>\n              </mrow>\n            </msub>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>,</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {\\frac {S_{\\text{BH}}}{k}}={\\frac {1}{4}}{\\frac {A}{A_{\\text{P}}}},}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2c48a2e1614a2eb40e6e5aeb4ca119fd2140f4d7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:14.564ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle {\\frac {S_{\\text{BH}}}{k}}={\\frac {1}{4}}{\\frac {A}{A_{\\text{P}}}},}"/></span></dd></dl>\n\nwhere <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle A_{\\text{P}}=\\hbar G/c^{3}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>A</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mtext>P</mtext>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mi class="MJX-variant">&#x210F;<!-- \xe2\x84\x8f --></mi>\n        <mi>G</mi>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <msup>\n          <mi>c</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mn>3</mn>\n          </mrow>\n        </msup>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle A_{\\text{P}}=\\hbar G/c^{3}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ac06457a0368343b53d60008680aedf7a1c5bf48" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.55ex; height:3.176ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle A_{\\text{P}}=\\hbar G/c^{3}}"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Planck_units#Derived_units" title="Planck units">Planck area</a> (the unit of area in quantum mechanics). Use of <a href="/wiki/Planck_units" title="Planck units">Planck units</a> (in which <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle k}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mi>k</mi>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle k}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c3c9a2c7b599b37105512c5d570edc034056dd40" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.211ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="k"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle A_{\\text{P}}}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>A</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mtext>P</mtext>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle A_{\\text{P}}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/130f657fb47d3f3cfdac0dfa95f321d09cf9b13b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.095ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle A_{\\text{P}}}"/></span> are set to unity) reduces it further to:\n\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle S_{\\text{BH}}={\\frac {A}{4}}.}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <msub>\n          <mi>S</mi>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mtext>BH</mtext>\n          </mrow>\n        </msub>\n        <mo>=</mo>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mfrac>\n            <mi>A</mi>\n            <mn>4</mn>\n          </mfrac>\n        </mrow>\n        <mo>.</mo>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle S_{\\text{BH}}={\\frac {A}{4}}.}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2104709467b60773575921f501c43f0ff019dd56" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:10.378ex; height:5.343ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle S_{\\text{BH}}={\\frac {A}{4}}.}"/></span></dd></dl>\n\n<a href="/wiki/Jacob_Bekenstein" title="Jacob Bekenstein">Jacob Bekenstein</a> had conjectured the proportionality; Hawking confirmed it and established the constant of proportionality at <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\\displaystyle 1/4}">\n  <semantics>\n    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n        <mn>1</mn>\n        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n          <mo>/</mo>\n        </mrow>\n        <mn>4</mn>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 1/4}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4d3cf1ef33695c3d98cb09f01e5700f927ce928c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.487ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="1/4"/></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian.Death_306-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian.Death-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Auto2J-10_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auto2J-10-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Calculations based on <a href="/wiki/String_theory" title="String theory">string theory</a>, first carried out in 1995, have been found to yield the same result.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup>\n\nThis relationship is conjectured to be valid not just for black holes, but also (since <a href="/wiki/Entropy_(information_theory)" title="Entropy (information theory)">entropy is proportional to information</a>) as an <a href="/wiki/Bekenstein_bound" title="Bekenstein bound">upper bound</a> on the amount of information that can be contained in any volume of space, which has in turn spawned deeper reflections on the possible <a href="/wiki/Holographic_principle" title="Holographic principle">nature of reality</a>.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-HawkingWestminster-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-HawkingWestminster_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-HawkingWestminster_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Shirbon, Estelle (20 March 2018). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.reuters.com/article/us-britain-hawking-ashes/stephen-hawking-to-join-newton-darwin-in-final-resting-place-idUSKBN1GW2GV">"Stephen Hawking to Join Newton, Darwin in Final Resting Place"</a>.
